href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Europe.svg" class="image"><img alt="Flag of Europe.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/32px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png" width="32" title="Portal:European Union">European Union&#32;portal</a> <div class="hlist" style="text-align:center;font-weight:normal;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_political_science#Politics_by_region" Union">Atlas</a></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_the_European_Union" title="Template:Politics of the European Union"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_the_European_Union" title="Template talk:Politics of the European Union"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>European integration</b> is the process of industrial, political, legal, <a href="/wiki/Economic_integration" title="Economic integration">economic</a>, social and cultural <a href="/wiki/Regional_integration" title="Regional integration">integration</a> of states wholly or partially in Europe. European integration has primarily come about through the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and its policies.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toclevel-1 tocsection-61"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-62"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>One of the first to conceive of a union of European nations was <a href="/wiki/Richard_von_Coudenhove-Kalergi" title="Richard von Coudenhove-Kalergi">Richard von Coudenhove-Kalergi</a>, who wrote the <a href="/wiki/Richard_von_Coudenhove-Kalergi#European_union" title="Richard von Coudenhove-Kalergi">Pan-Europa manifesto</a> in 1923.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> His ideas influenced <a href="/wiki/Aristide_Briand" title="Aristide Briand">Aristide Briand</a>, who gave a speech in favour of a European Union in the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> on 8 September 1929, and who in 1930 wrote a "Memorandum on the Organization of a Regime of European Federal Union" for the Government of France,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> which became the first European government formally to adopt the principle.\n</p>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: 59%;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">We must build a kind of United States of Europe. In this way only, will hundreds of millions of toilers be able to regain the simple joys and hopes which make life worth living.\n<p><i>Winston Churchill</i>\n<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n\n</tbody></table>\n<p>At the end of World War II, the continental political climate favoured unity in democratic European countries, seen by many as an escape from the extreme forms of nationalism which had devastated the continent.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In a speech delivered on 19 September 1946 at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Z%C3%BCrich" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Z\xc3\xbcrich">University of Z\xc3\xbcrich</a>, Switzerland, <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> postulated a <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_Europe" title="United States of Europe">United States of Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The same speech however contains remarks, less often quoted, which make it clear that Churchill did not initially see Britain as being part of this United States of Europe: <i>We British have our own Commonwealth of Nations ... And why should there not be a European group which could give a sense of enlarged patriotism and common citizenship to the distracted peoples of this turbulent and mighty continent and why should it not take its rightful place with other great groupings in shaping the destinies of men?</i> ... <i>France and Germany must take the lead together. Great Britain, the British Commonwealth of Nations, mighty America and I trust Soviet Russia-for then indeed all would be well-must be the friends and sponsors of the new Europe and must champion its right to live and shine.</i>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Theories_of_integration">Theories of integration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Theories of integration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The question of how to avoid wars between the nation-states was essential for the first theories. <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">Federalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Functionalism_in_international_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Functionalism in international relations">Functionalism</a> proposed the containment of the nation-state, while <b><a href="/wiki/Transactionalism" title="Transactionalism">Transactionalism</a></b> sought to theorise the conditions for the stabilisation of the nation-state system.\n</p><p>One of the most influential theories of European integration is <a href="/wiki/Neofunctionalism" title="Neofunctionalism">neofunctionalism</a>, developed by <a href="/wiki/Ernst_B._Haas" title="Ernst B. Haas">Ernst B. Haas</a> (1958) and further investigated by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Leon_Lindberg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Leon Lindberg (page does not exist)">Leon Lindberg</a> (1963). This theory focuses on spillovers of integration, which leads to more integration.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> By contrast, the other big influential theory in Integration Studies, Liberal Intergovernmentalism, focuses on state preferences  being realised through bargaining. This theory was developed by Andrew Moravcsik in the 1990s, by building on the \'intergovernmentalist\' work of Stanley Hoffman and others. It remains very influential.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The important debate between neofunctionalism and Liberal <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmentalism" title="Intergovernmentalism">intergovernmentalism</a> still remains central in understanding the development and setbacks of the European integration.\n</p><p>As the empirical world has changed, so have the theories and thus the understanding of European Integration. Today there is a relatively new focus on the complex policy-making in the EU and <a href="/wiki/Multi-level_governance" title="Multi-level governance">multi-level governance</a> (MLG) trying to produce a theory of the workings and development of the EU.\n</p><p>\nAccording to a 2016 study, European integration deepens through a "failing forward" process whereby,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></p><blockquote><p>Intergovernmental bargaining leads to incompleteness because it forces states with diverse preferences to settle on lowest common denominator solutions. Incompleteness then unleashes forces that lead to crisis. Member states respond by again agreeing to lowest common denominator solutions, which address the crisis and lead to deeper integration. To date, this sequential cycle of piecemeal reform, followed by policy failure, followed by further reform, has managed to sustain both the European project and the common currency. </p></blockquote>\n<h2><span id="Citizens.27_organisations_calling_for_further_integration"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Citizens\'_organisations_calling_for_further_integration">Citizens\' organisations calling for further integration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Citizens&#039; organisations calling for further integration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Various federalist organisations have been created over time supporting the idea of a federal Europe. These include the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_European_Federalists" title="Union of European Federalists">Union of European Federalists</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Movement_International" title="European Movement International">European Movement International</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Federalist_Party" title="European Federalist Party">European Federalist Party</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Union_of_European_Federalists" title="Union of European Federalists">Union of European Federalists</a> (UEF) is a European non-governmental organisation, campaigning for a Federal Europe. It consists of 20 constituent organisations and it has been active at the European, national and local levels for more than 50 years. The <a href="/wiki/European_Movement_International" title="European Movement International">European Movement International</a> is a lobbying association that coordinates the efforts of associations and national councils with the goal of promoting European integration, and disseminating information about it. The <a href="/wiki/European_Federalist_Party" title="European Federalist Party">European Federalist Party</a> is the pro-European, pan-European and federalist political party which advocates further integration of the EU and the establishment of a Federal Europe. Its aim is to gather all Europeans to promote European federalism and to participate in all elections all over Europe.  It has national sections in 15 countries.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overlap_of_membership_in_various_agreements">Overlap of membership in various agreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Overlap of membership in Several countries take part in a larger number of agreements than others.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Common_membership_of_member_states_of_the_European_Union">Common membership of member states of the European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Common membership of member states of the European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>All <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Member states of the European Union">member states of the European Union</a> (EU) are members of the:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE), Secretariat: Vienna, Austria</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> (CoE), HQ: Strasbourg, France</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Civil_Aviation_Conference" title="European Civil Aviation Conference">European Civil Aviation Conference</a> (ECAC), HQ: Neuilly-sur-Seine/Paris, France</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Organisation_for_the_Safety_of_Air_Navigation" class="mw-redirect" title="European Organisation for the Safety of Air Navigation">European Organisation for the Safety of Air Navigation</a> (Eurocontrol), HQ: Brussels, Belgium</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Committee_for_Standardization" title="European Committee for Standardization">European Committee for Standardization</a> (CEN), HQ: Brussels, Belgium</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Telecommunications_Standards_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="European Telecommunications Standards Institute">European Telecommunications Standards Institute</a> (ETSI), HQ: Sophia Antipolis, France</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Committee_for_Electrotechnical_Standardization" title="European Committee for Electrotechnical Standardization">European Committee for Electrotechnical Standardization</a> (CENELEC), HQ: Brussels, Belgium</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">European Union Customs Union</a> (EUCU)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Olympic_Committees" title="European Olympic Committees">European Olympic Committees</a> (EOC), HQ: Rome, Italy</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Patent_Convention" title="European Patent Convention">European Patent Convention</a> (EPC)/European Patent Organisation (EPOrg)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Atomic_Energy_Community" title="European Atomic Energy Community">European Atomic Energy Community</a> (EAEC, Euratom)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Single_Euro_Payments_Area" title="Single Euro Payments Area">Single Euro Payments Area</a> (SEPA)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Common_Aviation_Area" title="European Common Aviation Area">European Common Aviation Area</a> (ECAA)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Higher_Education_Area" title="European Higher Education Area">European Higher Education Area</a> (EHEA) - Belgium as <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Community" title="Flemish Community">Flemish Community</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_Community" title="French Community">French Community</a>, i.e. the <a href="/wiki/German-speaking_Community_of_Belgium" title="German-speaking Community of Belgium">German-speaking Community of Belgium</a> is not included.</li></ul>\n<p>have organizations that are members of the:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/European_Broadcasting_Union" title="European Broadcasting Union">European Broadcasting Union</a> (EBU), HQ: Geneva, Switzerland</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Union_of_European_Football_Associations" class="mw-redirect" title="Union of European Football Associations">Union of European Football Associations</a> (UEFA), HQ: Nyon, Switzerland</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Network_of_Transmission_System_Operators_for_Electricity" title="European Network of Transmission System Operators for Electricity">European Network of Transmission System Operators for Electricity</a>, HQ: Brussels, Belgium</li></ul>\n<p>have organisations that are members, associated partners or observers of the\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/European_Network_of_Transmission_System_Operators_for_Gas" title="European Network of Transmission System Operators for Gas">European Network of Transmission System Operators for Gas</a>, HQ: Brussels, Belgium</li></ul>\n<p>are located in the <a href="/wiki/European_Broadcasting_Area" title="European Broadcasting Area">European Broadcasting Area</a> (EBA)\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Most_integrated_countries">Most integrated countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Most integrated countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Fourteen states are part of the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> and <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>. These are Belgium, Estonia, France, Germany, Greece, Italy, Latvia, Lithuania, Luxembourg, the Netherlands, Portugal, Slovakia, Slovenia and Spain.\n</p><p>They are all members of:\n</p>\n<ul><li>the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a></li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a> (EEA)</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a></li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/European_Defence_Agency" title="European Defence Agency">European Defence Agency</a> (EDA)</li></ul>\n<p>Of these states several take part in further organisations, but some are outside.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable EMF)\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<p>France is part of all of these groups, and Belgium and Germany take part in all where at least half of the 14 member states participate.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_scope">Geographic scope</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geographic scope">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beyond_geographic_Europe">Beyond geographic Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Beyond geographic Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Some agreements that are mostly related to countries of the European continent, are also valid in territories outside the continent.\n</p><p>Not listed below are agreements if their scope is beyond geographic Europe only because the agreement includes:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Territories of transcontinental countries: Russia, Kazakhstan, Turkey, Azerbaijan, Armenia and Georgia contain some territory in Europe and some in Asia</li>\n<li>Special territories of European countries, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Special_territories_of_member_states_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Special territories of member states of the European Union">Special territories of member states of the European Union</a></li>\n<li>Cyprus, which is a member of the Council of Europe and several other agreements</li></ul>\n<p>List:\n</p>\n<ul><li>NATO contains USA and Canada, but has a European focus, Article 10 of the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty" title="North Atlantic Treaty">North Atlantic Treaty</a> describes how non-member states may join: "The Parties may [...] invite any other European State in a position to further the principles of this Treaty"<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE) contains USA, Canada, Central Asian countries and Mongolia</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Broadcasting_Union" title="European Broadcasting Union">European Broadcasting Union</a> (EBU) contains North African and Middle East countries</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Olympic_Committees" title="European Olympic Committees">European Olympic Committees</a> (EOC) contains <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Limited_to_regions_within_geographic_Europe">Limited to regions within geographic Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Limited to regions within geographic Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Several <a href="/wiki/Regional_integration" title="Regional integration">regional integration</a> efforts have effectively promoted intergovernmental cooperation and reduced the possibility of regional armed conflict. Other initiatives have removed barriers to free trade in European regions, and increased the free movement of people, labour, goods, and capital across national borders.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nordic_countries">Nordic countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Nordic countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Since the end of the Second World War, the following organisations have been established in the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Nordic region">Nordic region</a>:\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Council" title="Nordic Council">Nordic Council</a> and the Nordic Council of Ministers is a co-operation forum for the parliaments and governments of the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic countries</a> created in February 1953. It includes the states of Denmark, Finland, Iceland, Norway and Sweden, and their autonomous territories (<a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a>, Greenland and <a href="/wiki/%C3%85land" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc3\x85land">\xc3\x85land</a>).\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Passport_Union" title="Nordic Passport Union">Nordic Passport Union</a>, created in 1954 but implemented on 1 May 1958, establishes free movement across borders without passports for the countries\' citizens. It comprises Denmark, Sweden and Norway as foundational states; further, it includes Finland and Iceland since 24 September 1965, and the Danish autonomous territories of <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a> since 1 January 1966.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Baltic_Sea_region">Baltic Sea region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Baltic Sea region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The following political and/or economic organisations have been in the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_region" title="Baltic region">Baltic region</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Postmodernity" title="Postmodernity">post-modern era</a>:\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Assembly" title="Baltic Assembly">Baltic Assembly</a> aims to promote co-operation between the parliaments of the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a>, namely the Republics of Estonia, Latvia and Lithuania. The organisation was planned in <a href="/wiki/Vilnius" title="Vilnius">Vilnius</a> on 1 December 1990, and the three nations agreed to its structure and rules on 13 June 1994.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Free_Trade_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Baltic Free Trade Area">Baltic Free Trade Area</a> (BAFTA) was a trade agreement between Estonia, Lithuania and Latvia. It was signed on 13 September 1993 and came into force on 1 April 1994. The agreement was later extended to apply also to agricultural products, effective from 1 January 1997. BAFTA ceased to exist when its members joined the EU on 1 May 2004.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Baltic_Sea_States" title="Council of the Baltic Sea States">Council of the Baltic Sea States</a> (CBSS) was founded in 1992 to promote intergovernmental cooperation among <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> countries in questions concerning economy, civil society development, human rights issues, and nuclear and radiation safety. It has 12 members including <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> (since 1995), <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>.\n</p><p>In 2009 the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> approved the EU Strategy for the Baltic Sea Region (EUSBSR) following a communication from the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>. The EUSBSR was the first macro-regional strategy in Europe. The Strategy aims to reinforce cooperation within the Baltic Sea Region, to address challenges together, and to promote balanced development in the Region. The Strategy contributes to major EU policies, including <a href="/wiki/Europe_2020" title="Europe 2020">Europe 2020</a>, and reinforces integration within the Region.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nordic-Baltic_Eight">Nordic-Baltic Eight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Nordic-Baltic Eight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/NB8" class="mw-redirect" title="NB8">NB8</a></div>\n<h4><span id="Low_Countries_region_.28Benelux.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Low_Countries_region_(Benelux)">Low Countries region (Benelux)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Low Countries region (Benelux)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Since the end of the First World War the following unions have been set in the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a> region:\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a> is an economic and political union between Belgium, the Netherlands, and Luxembourg. On 5 September 1944, a treaty establishing the Benelux Customs Union was signed. It entered into force in 1948, and ceased to exist on 1 November 1960, when it was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Benelux_Economic_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Benelux Economic Union">Benelux Economic Union</a> after a treaty signed in The Hague on 3 February 1958. A <a href="/wiki/Benelux_Parliament" title="Benelux Parliament">Benelux Parliament</a> was created in 1955.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Belgium-Luxembourg_Economic_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgium-Luxembourg Economic Union">Belgium-Luxembourg Economic Union</a> (BLEU) can be seen as a forerunner of the Benelux. BLEU was created by the treaty signed on 25 July 1921. It established a <a href="/wiki/Single_market" title="Single market">single market</a> between both countries, while setting the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_franc" title="Belgian franc">Belgian franc</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luxembourgian_franc" class="mw-redirect" title="Luxembourgian franc">Luxembourgian franc</a> at a fixed parity.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Black_Sea_region">Black Sea region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Black Sea region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Several regional organisations have been founded in the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> region since the fall of the Soviet Union, such as:\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_the_Black_Sea_Economic_Cooperation" title="Organization of the Black Sea Economic Cooperation">Organization of the Black Sea Economic Cooperation</a> (BSEC) aims to ensure peace, stability and prosperity by encouraging friendly and good-neighbourly relations among the 12 state members, located mainly in the Black Sea region. It was created on 25 June 1992 in Istanbul, and entered into force on 1 May 1999. The 11 founding members were Albania, Armenia, Azerbaijan, Bulgaria, Georgia, Greece, Moldova, Romania, Russia, Turkey, and Ukraine. Serbia (then Serbia and Montenegro) joined in April 2004.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/GUAM_Organization_for_Democracy_and_Economic_Development" title="GUAM Organization for Democracy and Economic Development">GUAM Organization for Democracy and Economic Development</a> is a regional organisation of four post-Soviet states, which aims to promote cooperation and democratic values, ensure stable development, enhance international and regional security, and stepping up European integration. Current members include the four founding ones, namely, Georgia, Ukraine, Azerbaijan, and Moldova. Uzbekistan joined in 1999, and left in 2005.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Britain_and_Ireland">Britain and Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Britain and Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Since the end of the First World War, the following agreements have been signed in the Britain and Ireland and Irish region:\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/British-Irish_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="British-Irish Council">British-Irish Council</a> was created by the <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Belfast Agreement">Belfast Agreement</a> in 1998 to <i>"promote the harmonious and mutually beneficial development of the totality of relationships among the peoples of these islands"</i>. It was formally established on 2 December 1999. Its membership comprises Ireland, the United Kingdom, three of the <a href="/wiki/Countries_of_the_UK" class="mw-redirect" title="Countries of the UK">countries of the UK</a> (<a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, Scotland and Wales), and three British <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">Crown dependencies</a> (<a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a>). Because England does not have a <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">devolved government</a>, it is not represented on the Council as a separate entity.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Common_Travel_Area" title="Common Travel Area">Common Travel Area</a> is a passport-free zone established in 1922 that comprises Ireland, the United Kingdom, the Isle of Man, Jersey and Guernsey.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_Europe">Central Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Central Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:V4_Sunday.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/V4_Sunday.jpg/220px-V4_Sunday.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/V4_Sunday.jpg/330px-V4_Sunday.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/V4_Sunday.jpg/440px-V4_Sunday.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:V4_Sunday.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flags of Visegr\xc3\xa1d Group countries</div></div></div>\n<p>The following cooperation agreements have been signed in Central Europe:\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="Visegr\xc3\xa1d Group">Visegr\xc3\xa1d Group</a> is a Central-European alliance for cooperation and European integration, based on an ancient strategic alliance of core Central European countries. The Group originated in a summit meeting of <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>, Hungary and Poland held in the Hungarian castle town of <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d" title="Visegr\xc3\xa1d">Visegr\xc3\xa1d</a> on 15 February 1991. The Czech Republic and Slovakia became members after the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Dissolution of Czechoslovakia">dissolution of Czechoslovakia</a> in 1993.\n</p><p>In 1989, <a href="/wiki/Central_European_Initiative" title="Central European Initiative">Central European Initiative</a>, a forum of regional has been formed in Hungary.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/CEFTA" class="mw-redirect" title="CEFTA">Central European Free Trade Agreement</a> (CEFTA) is a trade agreement between countries in Central Europe and the Balkans, which works as a preparation for full European Union membership. As of  2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, it has 7 members: Macedonia, Albania, Bosnia and Herzegovina, Moldova, Montenegro, Serbia and <a href="/wiki/UNMIK" class="mw-redirect" title="UNMIK">UNMIK-administered Kosovo province</a>.\n</p><p>It was established in 1992 by <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>, Hungary and Poland, but came into force only in 1994. Czechoslovakia had in the meantime split into the Czech Republic and Slovakia. Slovenia joined in 1996, while Romania did the same in 1997, Bulgaria in 1999, and Croatia in 2003. In 2004, the Czech Republic, Slovakia, Hungary, Poland, and Slovenia left the CEFTA to join the EU. Romania and Bulgaria left it in 2007 for the same reason. Subsequently, Macedonia joined it in 2006, and Albania, Bosnia and Herzegovina, Moldova, Montenegro, Serbia and <a href="/wiki/UNMIK" class="mw-redirect" title="UNMIK">UNMIK</a> (on behalf of Kosovo) in 2007. In 2013, Croatia left the CEFTA to join the EU.\n</p><p><b>Switzerland and Liechtenstein</b> participate in a <a href="/wiki/Customs_union" title="Customs union">customs union</a> since 1924, and both employ the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_franc" title="Swiss franc">Swiss franc</a> as national currency.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Europe">Eastern Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Eastern Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The effects of the EU integration process of the countries from the former <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern bloc</a> are still debated. As a result, the relationship between immigration levels and EU public support remains uncertain. Through the integration, the countries in Eastern Europe have experienced growth of the economy, benefits of the free market agreements and freedom of the labor movement within the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> However, the results of the empirical socioeconomic analyses<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (June 2016)">which?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> suggest that in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, the immigration from CEE had negative effects on support for European integration in the host societies.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The research<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (June 2016)">which?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> also implies that the immigration from the CEE seems to undermine the long-term effects of the integration.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> There are theories<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (June 2016)">which?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> for the programs of social development that range in views from: an extended contact with the immigrants from <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> might help forge a common European identity and it could also lead to a potential national isolation, caused by tightening support mechanisms for the labor immigration.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Equal amount of research also implies that the internal migration of the countries within the EU is necessary for the successful development of its economic union.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Danube_region">Danube region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Danube region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The EU Strategy for the Danube Region was endorsed by the European Council in 2011 and is the second macro-regional strategy in Europe. The Strategy provides a basis for improved cooperation among 14 countries along the <a href="/wiki/Danube_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Danube River">Danube River</a>. It aims to improve the effectiveness of regional integration efforts and leverage the impact of policies at the EU, national and local levels.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Council_of_Europe">Council of Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Council of Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Council_of_Europe_map.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Council_of_Europe_map.svg/250px-Council_of_Europe_map.svg.png" width="250" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Council_of_Europe_map.svg/375px-Council_of_Europe_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Council_of_Europe_map.svg/500px-Council_of_Europe_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="940" data-file-height="415" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Council_of_Europe_map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #007800; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Ten founding members</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00ff00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Joined subsequently</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Official candidates</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ffff00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Observer at the Parliamentary Assembly</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff6600; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Observer at the Committee of Ministers</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #552200; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Observer at the Committee of Ministers and the Parliamentary Assembly</div></div></div></div>\n<p>Against the background of the devastation and human suffering during the Second World War as well as the need for reconciliation after the war, the idea of European integration led to the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> in <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a> in 1949.\n</p><p>The most important achievement of the Council of Europe is the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a> of 1950 with its <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Human_Rights" title="European Court of Human Rights">European Court of Human Rights</a> in Strasbourg, which serves as a <i>de facto</i> supreme court for human rights and fundamental freedoms throughout Europe. Human rights are also protected by the Council of Europe\'s <a href="/wiki/Committee_for_the_Prevention_of_Torture" title="Committee for the Prevention of Torture">Committee for the Prevention of Torture</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Social_Charter" title="European Social Charter">European Social Charter</a>.\n</p><p>Most conventions of the Council of Europe pursue the aim of greater legal integration, such as the conventions on legal assistance, against corruption, against <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a>, against <a href="/wiki/Doping_in_sport" title="Doping in sport">doping in sport</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Internet_crime" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet crime">internet crime</a>.\n</p><p>Cultural co-operation is based on the <a href="/wiki/Hague_Convention_for_the_Protection_of_Cultural_Property_in_the_Event_of_Armed_Conflict" title="Hague Convention for the Protection of Cultural Property in the Event of Armed Conflict">Cultural Convention of 1954</a> and subsequent conventions on the recognition of university studies and diplomas as well as on the protection of minority languages.\n</p><p>After the fall of the Berlin Wall, former communist European countries were able to accede to the Council of Europe, which now comprises 47 states in Europe. Therefore, European integration has practically succeeded at the level of the Council of Europe, encompassing almost the whole European continent, with the exception of Kazakhstan and Belarus, the latter due to its still non-democratic government.\n</p><p>European integration at the level of the Council of Europe functions through the accession of member states to its conventions as well as through political coordination at the level of ministerial conferences and inter-parliamentary sessions. In accordance with its Statute of 1949, the Council of Europe works to achieve greater unity among its members based on common values, such as human rights and democracy.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:612px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OSCEcountries.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/OSCEcountries.PNG/610px-OSCEcountries.PNG" width="610" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/OSCEcountries.PNG/915px-OSCEcountries.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/67/OSCEcountries.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1158" data-file-height="245" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OSCEcountries.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE) is a trans-Atlantic <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organization" title="Intergovernmental organization">intergovernmental organisation</a> whose aim is to secure stability in Europe. It was established as the <a href="/wiki/Conference_on_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Conference on Security and Co-operation in Europe">Conference on Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (CSCE) in July 1973, and was subsequently transformed into its current form in January 1995. The OSCE has 56 member states, covering most of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_hemisphere" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern hemisphere">northern hemisphere</a>.\n</p><p>The OSCE develops three lines of activities, namely the <i>Politico-Military Dimension</i>, the <i>Economic and Environmental Dimension</i> and the <i>Human Dimension</i>. These respectively promote (i) mechanisms for conflict prevention and resolution; (ii) the monitoring, alerting and assistance in case of economic and environmental threats; and (iii) full respect for human rights and fundamental freedoms.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Free_Trade_Association">European Free Trade Association</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: European Free Trade Association">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EFTA_AELE_countries.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/EFTA_AELE_countries.svg/200px-EFTA_AELE_countries.svg.png" width="200" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/EFTA_AELE_countries.svg/300px-EFTA_AELE_countries.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/EFTA_AELE_countries.svg/400px-EFTA_AELE_countries.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EFTA_AELE_countries.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>EFTA members</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association" title="European Free Trade Association">European Free Trade Association</a> (EFTA) is a European <a href="/wiki/Trade_bloc" title="Trade bloc">trade bloc</a> which was established on 3 May 1960 as an alternative for European states who did not join the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">EEC</a>. EFTA currently has four member states: Iceland, Norway, Switzerland, and Liechtenstein; just Norway and Switzerland are founding members.\n</p><p>The EFTA Convention was signed on 4 January 1960 in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a> by seven states: Austria, Denmark, Norway, Portugal, Sweden, Switzerland and the United Kingdom. Finland became an associate member in 1961 and a full member in 1986; Iceland joined in 1970 and Liechtenstein did the same in 1991.\n</p><p>The United Kingdom and Denmark left in 1973, when they joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="European Community">European Community</a> (EC). Portugal left EFTA in 1986, when it also joined the EC. Austria, Finland and Sweden ceased to be EFTA members in 1995 by joining the European Union, which superseded the EC in 1993.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Broadcasting_Union">European Broadcasting Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: European Broadcasting Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EBU_enlargement_animation.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/EBU_enlargement_animation.gif/200px-EBU_enlargement_animation.gif" width="200" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/EBU_enlargement_animation.gif/300px-EBU_enlargement_animation.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/EBU_enlargement_animation.gif/400px-EBU_enlargement_animation.gif 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="540" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EBU_enlargement_animation.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Countries with Active EBU Membership coloured in order of accession from 1950.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_Broadcasting_Union" title="European Broadcasting Union">European Broadcasting Union</a></div>\n<p>The European Broadcasting Union (EBU) is an alliance of public service media entities, established on 12 February 1950. As of  2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the organisation comprises 73 active members in 56 countries,<sup id="cite_ref-EBU_Active_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBU_Active-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and 34 associate members from a further 20 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-EBU_Associates_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBU_Associates-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Most EU states are part of this organisation and therefore EBU has been subject to <a href="/wiki/Supranational" class="mw-redirect" title="Supranational">supranational</a> legislation and regulation.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> It also hosted debates between candidates for the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Union" title="President of the European Union">presidency</a> for the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2014" title="European Parliament election, 2014">2014 parliamentary elections</a> but is unrelated to the institution itself.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Patent_Convention">European Patent Convention</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: European Patent Convention">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Office_europeen_brevets.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Office_europeen_brevets.svg/200px-Office_europeen_brevets.svg.png" width="200" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Office_europeen_brevets.svg/300px-Office_europeen_brevets.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Office_europeen_brevets.svg/400px-Office_europeen_brevets.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Office_europeen_brevets.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>EPC contracting states and the extension states, Bosnia and Herzegovina and Montenegro.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_Patent_Convention" title="European Patent Convention">European Patent Convention</a></div>\n<p>As of 2013 there are 38 parties to European Patent Convention. The Convention on the Grant of European Patents was first signed on 5 October 1973.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Communities">European Communities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: European Communities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 1951, Belgium, France, Italy, Luxembourg, the Netherlands and West Germany agreed to confer powers over their steel and coal production to the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a> (ECSC) in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1951)" title="Treaty of Paris (1951)">Treaty of Paris</a>, which came into force on 23 July 1952.\n</p><p>Coal and steel production was essential for the reconstruction of countries in Europe after the Second World War and this sector of the national economy had been important for warfare in the First and Second World Wars. Therefore, France had originally maintained its occupation of the <a href="/wiki/Saarland" title="Saarland">Saarland</a> with its steel companies after the founding of the Federal Republic of Germany (West Germany) in 1949. By transferring national powers over the coal and steel production to a newly created ECSC Commission, the member states of the ECSC were able to provide for greater transparency and trust among themselves.\n</p><p>This transfer of national powers to a "Community" to be exercised by its Commission was paralleled under the 1957 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome" title="Treaty of Rome">Treaty of Rome</a> establishing the <a href="/wiki/European_Atomic_Energy_Community" title="European Atomic Energy Community">European Atomic Energy Community</a> (or Euratom) and the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (EEC) in Brussels.\n</p><p>In 1967, the <a href="/wiki/Merger_Treaty" title="Merger Treaty">Merger Treaty</a> (or <b>Brussels Treaty</b>) combine the institutions of the ECSC and Euratom into that of the EEC. They already shared a <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">Parliamentary Assembly</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Justice" title="European Court of Justice">Courts</a>. Collectively they were known as the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a>. In 1987, the <a href="/wiki/Single_European_Act" title="Single European Act">Single European Act</a> (SEA) was the first major revision of the Treaty of Rome that formally established the single European market and the European Political Cooperation. The Communities originally had independent personalities although they were increasingly integrated, and over the years were transformed into what is now called the European Union.\n</p><p>The six states that founded the three Communities were known as the "<a href="/wiki/Inner_six" class="mw-redirect" title="Inner six">inner six</a>" (the "outer seven" were those countries who formed the <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association" title="European Free Trade Association">European Free Trade Association</a>). These were Belgium, France, Italy, Luxembourg, the Netherlands, and West Germany. The first enlargement was in 1973, with the accession of Denmark, Ireland and the United Kingdom. Greece joined in 1981, and Portugal and Spain in 1986. On 3 October 1990 East Germany and West Germany were reunified, hence East Germany became part of the Community in the new reunified Germany (not increasing the number of states).\n</p><p>A key person in the Community creation process was <a href="/wiki/Jean_Monnet" title="Jean Monnet">Jean Monnet</a>, regarded as the "founding father" of the European Union, which is seen as the dominant force in European integration.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Martin_Schulz" title="Martin Schulz">Martin Schulz</a> proposed the abolition of the <a href="/wiki/National_parliaments_of_the_European_Union" title="National parliaments of the European Union">National parliaments of the European Union</a> and their replacement by the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> for the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_Europe" title="United States of Europe">United States of Europe</a> where every <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">Head of government</a> will be appointed by the representative of every <a href="/wiki/Party_leader" title="Party leader">Party leader</a> who gained the larger precentage of votes in their native country compared to the respective ones in every other <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">Member state of the European Union</a> running on behalf of the same <a href="/wiki/European_political_party" title="European political party">European political party</a>, to every country where a <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">Political party</a> under the same <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_group" title="Parliamentary group">Parliamentary group</a> has won the first place in the <a href="/wiki/Elections_to_the_European_Parliament" title="Elections to the European Parliament">Elections to the European Parliament</a>, which will happen every five years with no possiblity for a <a href="/wiki/Snap_election" title="Snap election">Snap election</a>. Every <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">Political party</a> not participating in a <a href="/wiki/European_political_party" title="European political party">European political party</a> will not be allowed to participate in the <a href="/wiki/Elections_to_the_European_Parliament" title="Elections to the European Parliament">Elections to the European Parliament</a>, thus essentialy preventing it from participating in <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">Government</a>.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.theguardian.com/world/2017/dec/07/martin-schulz-united-states-of-europe-germany-sdp">[6]</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (September 2018)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Single_Market_integration.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/European_Single_Market_integration.svg/300px-European_Single_Market_integration.svg.png" width="300" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/European_Single_Market_integration.svg/450px-European_Single_Market_integration.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/European_Single_Market_integration.svg/600px-European_Single_Market_integration.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Single_Market_integration.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Participation in the <a href="/wiki/European_Single_Market" title="European Single Market">European Single Market</a> of the EU:<span style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:1px; font-size:90%; text-align:left; display:block;"><span style="border:#3F48CC solid 1px;; background-color:#3F48CC; color:#3F48CC">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Member states of the European Union">European Union member states</a> form the European Single Market</span><span style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:1px; font-size:90%; text-align:left; display:block;"><span style="border:#3dc1ed solid 1px;; background-color:#3dc1ed; color:#3dc1ed">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>&#160;Non-EU states that participate in the EU Single Market with exceptions: <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> (see also <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association" title="European Free Trade Association">EFTA</a>)</span><span style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:1px; font-size:90%; text-align:left; display:block;"><span style="border:#48cc3f solid 1px;; background-color:#48cc3f; color:#48cc3f">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>&#160;Non-EU states with a <a href="/wiki/Stabilisation_and_Association_Process" title="Stabilisation and Association Process">Stabilisation and Association Agreement</a> with the EU allowing for participation in selected sectors of the Single Market: EU accession candidates <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>; potential EU accession candidates: <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a></span><span style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:1px; font-size:90%; text-align:left; display:block;"><span style="border:#FFD833 solid 1px;; background-color:#FFD833; color:#FFD833">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>&#160;Non-EU states which have a bilateral Customs Union arrangement with the EU: <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a> and EU accession candidate <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a></span><span style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:1px; font-size:90%; text-align:left; display:block;"><span style="border:#ff8c00 solid 1px;; background-color:#ff8c00; color:#ff8c00">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>&#160;Non-EU states with a <a href="/wiki/Deep_and_Comprehensive_Free_Trade_Area" title="Deep and Comprehensive Free Trade Area">Deep and Comprehensive Free Trade Area</a> agreement with the EU allowing for participation in selected sectors of the Single Market: <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a></span></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">Enlargement of the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Future enlargement of the European Union">Future enlargement of the European Union</a></div>\n<p>The European Union (EU) is an association of twenty-eight sovereign <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Member states of the European Union">member states</a>, that by treaty have delegated certain of their competences to common institutions, in order to coordinate their policies in a number of areas, without however constituting a new state on top of the member states. Officially established by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Maastricht" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Maastricht">Treaty of Maastricht</a> in 1993 upon the foundations of the pre-existing <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a>.\n</p><p>Thus, 12 states are founding members, namely, Belgium, Denmark, France, Germany, Greece,  Ireland, Italy, Luxembourg, the Netherlands, Portugal, Spain, and the United Kingdom. In 1995, Austria, Finland and Sweden entered the EU. Cyprus, the Czech Republic, Estonia, Hungary, Latvia, Lithuania, Malta, Poland, Slovakia, and Slovenia joined in 2004. Bulgaria and Romania joined in 2007. Croatia acceded in 2013. Official candidate states include Albania, Macedonia,<sup id="cite_ref-FYROM_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FYROM-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Montenegro, Serbia and Turkey. Morocco\'s application was rejected by the EEC, Iceland\'s application is withdrawn by government and Switzerland\'s is frozen.  Norway rejected membership in two referendums.\n</p><p>The institutions of the European Union, its parliamentarians, judges, commissioners and secretariat, the governments of its member states as well as their people, all play a role in European Integration. Nevertheless, the question of who plays the key role is disputed as there are different theories on European Integration focusing on different actors and agency.\n</p><p>The European Union has a number of relationships with nations that are not formally part of the Union. According to the European Union\'s official site, and a statement by Commissioner G\xc3\xbcnter Verheugen, the aim is to have a ring of countries, sharing EU\'s democratic ideals and joining them in further integration without necessarily becoming full member states.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competences">Competences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Competences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Member_State_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Member State of the European Union">Member State of the European Union</a></div>\n<p>Whilst most responsibilities (\'competences\') are retained by the member states, some competences are conferred exclusively on the Union for collective decision, some are shared pending Union action and some receive Union support.  These are shown on this table:\n</p>\n<table style="width:100%;background:none;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td colspan="4" style="font-size:89%;text-align:center;">As outlined in <a title="s:Consolidated version of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union/Part One: Principles">Title I of Part I of the consolidated Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union</a> style="font-size:90%;vertical-align:top;text-align:left;">\n<td style="background:#bac6f4;padding-bottom:5px;">\n<div><ul><li style="line-height:1.2em;">the <a href="/wiki/European_Single_Market"
