href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_European_Union" title="Transport in the European Union">transport</a></li><li style="line-height:1.2em;"><a href="/wiki/Trans-European_Networks" title="Trans-European Networks">trans-European networks</a></li><li style="line-height:1.2em;"><a href="/wiki/Energy_policy_of_the_European_Union" title="Energy policy of the European Union">energy</a></li><li style="line-height:1.2em;">the <a href="/wiki/Area_of_freedom,_security_and_justice" title="Area of freedom, security and justice">area of freedom, security and justice</a></li><li style="line-height:1.2em;">common safety concerns in public health matters, for the aspects defined in this Treaty</li></ul></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td>\n<td style="width:25%;vertical-align:top;">\n<table width="100%" border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="2" style="padding-top:5px;">\n\n<tbody><tr style="font-size:90%;text-align:center;">\n<td style="background:#bac6f4;padding:5px;line-height:1.2em;border-bottom:2px dotted white;">"<i>Union exercise of competence shall not result in Member States being prevented from exercising theirs in</i>"&#160;\xe2\x80\xa6\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="font-size:90%;vertical-align:top;text-align:left;">\n<td style="background:#bac6f4;padding-bottom:5px;border-bottom:4px solid white;">\n<div><ul><li style="line-height:1.2em;">research, technological development and&#160;<a href="/wiki/European_Space_Policy" class="mw-redirect" title="European Space Policy">(outer) space</a></li><li style="line-height:1.2em;">development cooperation, humanitarian aid</li></ul></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table width="100%" border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="2">\n\n<tbody><tr style="font-size:90%;text-align:center;">\n<td style="background:#bac6f4;padding:5px;line-height:1.2em;border-bottom:2px dotted white;">"<i>The Union coordinates Member States policies or implements supplemental to theirs common policies, not covered elsewhere</i>"\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="font-size:90%;vertical-align:top;text-align:left;">\n<td style="background:#bac6f4;padding-bottom:5px;">\n<div><ul><li style="line-height:1.2em;">coordination of economic, employment and social policies</li><li style="line-height:1.2em;">common <a href="/wiki/Common_Foreign_and_Security_Policy" title="Common Foreign and Security Policy">foreign, security</a> and <a href="/wiki/Common_Security_and_Defence_Policy" title="Common Security and Defence Policy">defence</a> policies</li></ul></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td>\n<td style="width:25%;vertical-align:top;">\n<table width="100%" border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="2" style="padding-top:5px;">\n\n<tbody><tr style="font-size:90%;text-align:center;">\n<td style="background:#e6ecfd;padding:5px;line-height:1.2em;border-bottom:2px dotted white;">"<i>The Union can carry out actions to support, coordinate or supplement Member States\' actions in</i>"&#160;\xe2\x80\xa6\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="font-size:90%;vertical-align:top;text-align:left;">\n<td style="background:#e6ecfd;padding-bottom:5px;">\n<div><ul><li style="line-height:1.2em;">the protection and improvement of human health</li><li style="line-height:1.2em;">industry</li><li style="line-height:1.2em;"><a href="/wiki/Cultural_policies_of_the_European_Union" title="Cultural policies of the European Union">culture</a></li><li style="line-height:1.2em;">tourism</li><li style="line-height:1.2em;"><a href="/wiki/Educational_policies_and_initiatives_of_the_European_Union" title="Educational policies and initiatives of the European Union">education</a>, youth, <a href="/wiki/Sport_policies_of_the_European_Union" title="Sport policies of the European Union">sport</a> and vocational training</li><li style="line-height:1.2em;">civil protection (disaster prevention)</li><li style="line-height:1.2em;">administrative cooperation</li></ul></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_integration">Economic integration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Economic integration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_European_Union" title="Economy of the European Union">Economy of the European Union</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Third_country_economic_relationships_with_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Third country economic relationships with the European Union">Third country economic relationships with the European Union</a></div>\n<p>The European Union operates a single economic market across the territory of all its members, and uses a single currency between the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> members. Further, the EU has a number of economic relationships with nations that are not formally part of the Union through the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a> and custom union agreements.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Free_trade_area">Free trade area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Free trade area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_free_trade_agreements.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/EU_free_trade_agreements.PNG/400px-EU_free_trade_agreements.PNG" width="400" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/EU_free_trade_agreements.PNG/600px-EU_free_trade_agreements.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/EU_free_trade_agreements.PNG/800px-EU_free_trade_agreements.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="625" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_free_trade_agreements.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/European_Union_free_trade_agreements" title="European Union free trade agreements">EU Free trade agreements</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The creation of the EEC eliminated tariffs, quotas and preferences on goods among member states, which are the requisites to define a <a href="/wiki/Free_trade_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Free trade area">free trade area</a> (FTA).\n</p><p>Numerous countries have signed a <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Association_Agreement" title="European Union Association Agreement">European Union Association Agreement</a> (AA) with FTA provisions. These mainly include Mediterranean countries (Algeria in 2005, Egypt in 2004, Israel in 2000, Jordan in 2002, Lebanon in 2006, Morocco in 2000, <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority" title="Palestinian National Authority">Palestinian National Authority</a> in 1997, and Tunisia in 1998), albeit some countries from other trade blocs have also signed one (such as Chile in 2003, Mexico in 2000, and South Africa in 2000).\n</p><p>Further, many Balkan states have signed a <a href="/wiki/Stabilisation_and_Association_Process" title="Stabilisation and Association Process">Stabilisation and Association Agreement</a> (SAA) with FTA provisions, such as Albania (signed 2006), Montenegro (2007), Macedonia (2004), Bosnia and Herzegovina and Serbia (both 2008, entry-into-force pending).\n</p><p>In 2008, Poland and Sweden proposed the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Partnership" title="Eastern Partnership">Eastern Partnership</a> which would include setting a FTA between the EU and Armenia, Azerbaijan, Belarus,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Georgia, Moldova and Ukraine.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Customs_union">Customs union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Customs union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">European Union Customs Union</a> defines an area where no customs are levied on goods travelling within it. It includes all <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Member states of the European Union">member states of the European Union</a>. The abolition of internal tariff barriers between <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">EEC</a> member states was achieved in 1968.\n</p><p>Andorra and San Marino belong to the EU customs unions with third states. Turkey is linked by the <a href="/wiki/European_Union-Turkey_Customs_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="European Union-Turkey Customs Union">European Union-Turkey Customs Union</a>.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Single_market">European Single market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: European Single market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>A prominent goal of the EU since its creation by the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a> in 1992 is establishing and maintaining a <a href="/wiki/Single_market" title="Single market">single market</a>. This seeks to guarantee the <a href="/wiki/Four_Freedoms_(European_Union)" class="mw-redirect" title="Four Freedoms (European Union)">four basic freedoms</a>, which are related to ensure the free movement of goods, services, capital and people around the EU\'s internal market.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a> (EEA) agreement allows Norway, Iceland and Liechtenstein to participate in the European Single Market without joining the EU. The four basic freedoms apply. However, some restrictions on fisheries and agriculture take place. Switzerland is linked to the European Union by <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_and_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Switzerland and the European Union">Swiss-EU bilateral agreements</a>, with a different content from that of the EEA agreement.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Eurozone">Eurozone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Eurozone">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Europ%C3%A4ische_Wirtschafts-_und_W%C3%A4hrungsunion.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Europ%C3%A4ische_Wirtschafts-_und_W%C3%A4hrungsunion.svg/220px-Europ%C3%A4ische_Wirtschafts-_und_W%C3%A4hrungsunion.svg.png" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Europ%C3%A4ische_Wirtschafts-_und_W%C3%A4hrungsunion.svg/330px-Europ%C3%A4ische_Wirtschafts-_und_W%C3%A4hrungsunion.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Europ%C3%A4ische_Wirtschafts-_und_W%C3%A4hrungsunion.svg/440px-Europ%C3%A4ische_Wirtschafts-_und_W%C3%A4hrungsunion.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Europ%C3%A4ische_Wirtschafts-_und_W%C3%A4hrungsunion.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Economic_and_Monetary_Union_of_the_European_Union" title="Economic and Monetary Union of the European Union">Economic and Monetary Union of the European Union</a> (2014) <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #003399; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Members of the Eurozone</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #e8984d; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;ERM-II-member with opt-out (Denmark)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #c34f4f; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;EU-member with opt-out (United Kingdom)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #704c4c; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;The rest of the EU-members, which are obliged to join</div></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> refers to the European Union member states that have adopted the euro <a href="/wiki/Currency_union" title="Currency union">currency union</a> as the third stage of the <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_Monetary_Union_of_the_European_Union" title="Economic and Monetary Union of the European Union">European Economic and Monetary Union</a> (EMU). Further, certain states outside the EU have adopted the euro as their currency, despite not belonging to the EMU. Thus, a total of 25 states, including 19 European Union states and six non-EU members, currently use the euro.\n</p><p>The Eurozone came into existence with the official launch of the euro on 1 January 1999. Physical <a href="/wiki/Euro_coins" title="Euro coins">coins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Euro_banknotes" title="Euro banknotes">banknotes</a> were introduced on 1 January 2002.\n</p><p>The original members were Austria, Belgium, Finland, France, Germany, Ireland, Italy, Luxembourg, the Netherlands, Portugal, and Spain. Greece adopted the euro on 1 January 2001. Slovenia joined on 1 January 2007, Cyprus and Malta were admitted on 1 January 2008, Slovakia joined on 1 January 2009, Estonia on 1 January 2011, Latvia on 1 January 2014 and Lithuania on 1 January 2015.\n</p><p>Outside the EU, agreements have been concluded with Andorra, Monaco, San Marino, and Vatican City for formal adoption, including the right to issue their own coins. Montenegro and Kosovo unilaterally adopted the euro when it launched.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fiscal_union">Fiscal union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Fiscal union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_Fiscal_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="European Fiscal Union">European Fiscal Union</a></div>\n<p>There has long been speculation about the possibility of the European Union eventually becoming a <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_union" title="Fiscal union">fiscal union</a>. In the wake of the <a href="/wiki/2010_European_sovereign_debt_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 European sovereign debt crisis">European sovereign debt crisis</a>, calls for closer fiscal ties, possibly leading to some sort of fiscal union have increased; though it is generally regarded as implausible in the short term, some analysts regard fiscal union as a long-term necessity.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> While stressing the need for coordination, governments have rejected talk of fiscal union or harmonisation in this regard.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aviation">Aviation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Aviation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:European_aviation_organisations_members.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="legend" title="European Common Aviation Area">ECAA</a></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" href="/wiki/European_Civil_Aviation_Conference" title="European Civil Aviation Conference">ECAC</a></div></div></div></div>\n<p>There are three main aviation related institutions present in Europe:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/European_Civil_Aviation_Conference" title="European Civil Aviation Conference">European Civil Aviation Conference (ECAC)</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eurocontrol" title="Eurocontrol">Eurocontrol</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Common_Aviation_Area" title="European Common Aviation Area">European Common Aviation Area (ECAA)</a></li></ul>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Energy_Community.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Energy_Community.svg/220px-Energy_Community.svg.png" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Energy_Community.svg/330px-Energy_Community.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Energy_Community.svg/440px-Energy_Community.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="589" data-file-height="468" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Energy_Community.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Energy Community in 2014 - Contracting Parties in dark blue, Observers in light blue</div></div></div>\n<p>The transnational energy related structures present in Europe are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Energy_Community" title="Energy Community">Energy Community</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Atomic_Energy_Community" title="European Atomic Energy Community">European Atomic Energy Community</a></li>\n<li><a Operators for Electricity</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Network_of_Transmission_System_Operators_for_Gas" title="European Network of Transmission System Operators for Gas">European Network of Transmission System Operators for Gas</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/INOGATE" title="INOGATE">INOGATE</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Energy_Charter_Treaty" title="Energy Charter Treaty">Energy Charter Treaty</a></li></ul>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Standardisation">Standardisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Standardisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The transnational standardisation organisations present in Europe are:\n</p>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/European_Telecommunications_Standards_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="European Telecommunications Standards Institute">European Telecommunications Standards Institute (ETSI)</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Committee_for_Standardization" title="European Committee for Standardization">European Committee for Standardization (CEN)</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Committee_for_Electrotechnical_Standardization" title="European Committee for Electrotechnical Standardization">European Committee for Electrotechnical Standardization (CENELEC)</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Reference_Materials_and_Measurements" title="Institute for Reference Materials and Measurements">Institute for Reference Materials and Measurements (IRMM)</a></li></ul>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_and_political_integration">Social and political integration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Social and political integration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/ERASMUS_programme" class="mw-redirect" title="ERASMUS programme">ERASMUS programme</a> (<b>E</b>uropean <b>R</b>egion <b>A</b>ction <b>S</b>cheme for the <b>M</b>obility of <b>U</b>niversity <b>S</b>tudents) seeks to encourage and support free movement of the academic community. It was established in 1987.\n</p><p>A total of 33 states (including all European Union states, Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway, Switzerland and Turkey) are involved.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EHEA.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/EHEA.PNG/400px-EHEA.PNG" width="400" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/EHEA.PNG/600px-EHEA.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e2/EHEA.PNG 2x" data-file-width="785" data-file-height="201" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EHEA.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/European_Higher_Education_Area" title="European Higher Education Area">European Higher Education Area</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Higher_Education_Area" title="European Higher Education Area">European Higher Education Area</a> (<b>EHEA</b>) aims to integrate education systems in Europe. Thus, degrees and study periods are recognised mutually. This is done by following the <a href="/wiki/Bologna_process" class="mw-redirect" title="Bologna process">Bologna process</a>, and under the <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Recognition_Convention" title="Lisbon Recognition Convention">Lisbon Recognition Convention</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>.\n</p><p>The Bologna declaration was signed in 1999 by 29 countries, all EU members or candidates at the moment (except Cyprus which joined later) and three out of four EFTA countries: Austria, Belgium, Bulgaria, Czech Republic, Denmark, Estonia, Finland, France, Germany, Greece, Hungary, Iceland, Ireland, Italy, Latvia, Lithuania, Luxembourg, Malta, the Netherlands, Norway, Poland, Portugal, Romania, Slovakia, Slovenia, Spain, Sweden, Switzerland, and United Kingdom. Croatia, Cyprus, Liechtenstein, and Turkey joined in 2001. In 2003, Albania, Andorra, Bosnia and Herzegovina, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> permanent observer), Macedonia, Russia, and Serbia signed the convention. Armenia, Azerbaijan, Georgia, Moldova and Ukraine followed in 2005. Montenegro joined in 2007. Finally, Kazakhstan (not a member of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>) joined in 2010. This makes a total of 47 member states. Monaco and San Marino are the only members of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> which have not adopted the convention. The other European nation that is eligible to join, but has not, is Belarus.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>There are a number of multinational research institutions based in Europe. Of these, eight are engaged in the <span style="background: lightblue"> <a href="/wiki/EIROforum" class="mw-redirect" title="EIROforum">EIROforum</a> collaboration. </span>\n</p>\n<div>\n\n&#32;\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;"><tbody><tr>\n<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<ul><li><span style="background: lightblue"> <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a> </span></li>\n<li><span style="background: lightblue"> <a href="/wiki/European_Molecular_Biology_Laboratory" title="European Molecular Biology Laboratory">European Molecular Biology Laboratory</a> </span></li>\n<li><span style="background: lightblue"> <a href="/wiki/European_Fusion_Development_Agreement" title="European Fusion Development Agreement">European Fusion Development Agreement</a> </span></li>\n<li><span style="background: lightblue"> <a href="/wiki/European_Southern_Observatory" title="European Southern Observatory">European Southern Observatory</a> </span></li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<p><b>Particle physics:</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><span style="background: lightblue"> <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">CERN</a> </span></li>\n<li><span style="background: lightblue"> <a href="/wiki/European_Synchrotron_Radiation_Facility" title="European Synchrotron Radiation Facility">European Synchrotron Radiation Facility</a> </span></li>\n<li><span style="background: lightblue"> <a href="/wiki/Institut_Laue%E2%80%93Langevin" title="Institut Laue\xe2\x80\x93Langevin">Institut Laue\xe2\x80\x93Langevin</a> </span></li>\n<li><span style="background: lightblue"> <a href="/wiki/European_XFEL" title="European XFEL">European XFEL</a> </span></li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<p><b>Meteorology:</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/EUMETSAT" class="mw-redirect" title="EUMETSAT">EUMETSAT</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Centre_for_Medium-Range_Weather_Forecasts" title="European Centre for Medium-Range Weather Forecasts">European Centre for Medium-Range Weather Forecasts</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/EUMETNET" title="EUMETNET">EUMETNET</a></li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:488px;max-width:488px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:252px;max-width:252px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_and_EFTA.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/EU_and_EFTA.svg/250px-EU_and_EFTA.svg.png" width="250" height="199" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/EU_and_EFTA.svg/375px-EU_and_EFTA.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/EU_and_EFTA.svg/500px-EU_and_EFTA.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="540" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">EHIC participating nations (EU members in blue, non-members in green)</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:232px;max-width:232px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Smart_Open_Services_nations.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Smart_Open_Services_nations.svg/230px-Smart_Open_Services_nations.svg.png" width="230" height="193" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Smart_Open_Services_nations.svg/345px-Smart_Open_Services_nations.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Smart_Open_Services_nations.svg/460px-Smart_Open_Services_nations.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2045" data-file-height="1720" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">epSOS participating nations</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Health_Insurance_Card" title="European Health Insurance Card">European Health Insurance Card</a> (or <b>EHIC</b>) is issued free of charge and allows anyone who is insured by or covered by a statutory social security scheme of the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">EEA</a> countries and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> to receive medical treatment in another member state for free or at a reduced cost, if that treatment becomes necessary during their visit (for example, due to illness or an accident), or if they have a chronic <a href="/wiki/Pre-existing_condition" title="Pre-existing condition">pre-existing condition</a> which requires care such as <a href="/wiki/Kidney_dialysis" class="mw-redirect" title="Kidney dialysis">kidney dialysis</a>.\n</p><p>The <b>epSOS</b> project, also known as <i>Smart Open Services for European Patients</i>, aims to promote free movement of patients.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> It will allow health professionals to electronically access the data from patients from another country, to electronically process prescriptions in all involved countries, or to provide treatment in another EU state to a patient on a waiting list.\n</p><p>The project has been launched by the EU and 47 member institutions from 23 EU member states and 3 non-EU members. They include national health ministries, national competence centres, social insurance institutions and scientific institutions as well as technical and administrative management entities.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights">Charter of Fundamental Rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Charter of Fundamental Rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights_of_the_European_Union" title="Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union">Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union</a> is a document enshrining certain <a href="/wiki/Fundamental_rights" title="Fundamental rights">fundamental rights</a>. The wording of the document has been agreed at ministerial level and has been incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a>. Poland and the United Kingdom have negotiated an opt out from this Charter.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Right_to_vote">Right to vote</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Right to vote">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The European integration process has extended the <a href="/wiki/Right_of_foreigners_to_vote" title="Right of foreigners to vote">right of foreigners to vote</a>. Thus, European Union citizens were given <a href="/wiki/Voting_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Voting rights">voting rights</a> in <a href="/wiki/Local_election" title="Local election">local elections</a> by the 1992 <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a>. Several member states (Belgium, Luxembourg, Lithuania, and Slovenia) have extended since then the right to vote to all foreign residents. This was already the case in Denmark, Finland, the Netherlands and Sweden. Further, voting and eligibility rights are granted among citizens of the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Passport_Union" title="Nordic Passport Union">Nordic Passport Union</a>, and between numerous countries through bilateral treaties (i.e. between Norway and Spain, or between Portugal and Brazil, Cape Verde, Iceland, Norway, Uruguay, Venezuela, Chile and Argentina), or without them (i.e. Ireland and the United Kingdom). Finally, within the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">EEA</a>, Iceland and Norway also grant the right to vote to all foreign residents.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Schengen_zone">Schengen zone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Schengen zone">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schengenzone.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Schengenzone.svg/220px-Schengenzone.svg.png" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Schengenzone.svg/330px-Schengenzone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Schengenzone.svg/440px-Schengenzone.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="645" data-file-height="690" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schengenzone.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Agreement</a> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #333366; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Full Schengen EU members</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #6666CC; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Non-EU Schengen members</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #CCCC00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Future members</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #336633; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Cooperating countries</div></div></div></div>\n<p>The main purpose of the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Agreement</a> is the abolition of physical borders among European countries. A total of 30 states, including 26 European Union states (all except Ireland and United Kingdom) and four non-EU members (Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway, and Switzerland), are subject to the Schengen rules. Its provisions have already been implemented by 26 states, leaving just Bulgaria, Croatia, Cyprus, and Romania to do so among signatory states.\n</p><p>Further, Monaco, San Marino and Vatican City are <i>de facto</i> members.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Visa_policy_in_EU">Visa policy in EU</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Visa policy in EU">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Visa_policy_of_the_Schengen_Area" title="Visa policy of the Schengen Area">Visa policy of the Schengen Area</a></div>\n<p>European Union has visa-free regime agreements with some European countries outside EU and discussing such agreements with others; Russia,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Ukraine,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> and Moldova.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Matters concerning Turkey have also been debated.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Ireland and the United Kingdom maintain independent visa policies in the EU.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of the European Union">Military of the European Union</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NATO_CSTO.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/NATO_CSTO.PNG/400px-NATO_CSTO.PNG" width="400" height="85" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/NATO_CSTO.PNG/600px-NATO_CSTO.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/NATO_CSTO.PNG/800px-NATO_CSTO.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1158" data-file-height="245" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NATO_CSTO.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> members in blue, <a href="/wiki/CSTO" class="mw-redirect" title="CSTO">CSTO</a> members in orange</div></div></div>\n<p>There are a number of multi-national military and peacekeeping forces which are ultimately under the command of the EU, and therefore can be seen as the core for a future European Union army.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> These corps include forces from 26 EU states \xe2\x80\x93 all except Denmark, which has an opt-out clause in its accession treaty and is not obliged to participate in the common defence policy; and Malta, which currently does not participate in any battlegroup \xe2\x80\x93, Norway and Turkey. Further, the <b><a href="/wiki/WEU" class="mw-redirect" title="WEU">Western European Union</a></b> (WEU) capabilities and functions have been transferred to the European Union, under its developing <a href="/wiki/Common_Foreign_and_Security_Policy" title="Common Foreign and Security Policy">Common Foreign and Security Policy</a> (CFSP) and <a href="/wiki/European_Security_and_Defence_Policy" class="mw-redirect" title="European Security and Defence Policy">European Security and Defence Policy</a> (ESDP).<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The EU also has close ties with the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">North Atlantic Treaty Organization</a> (NATO), according to the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Plus_agreement" title="Berlin Plus agreement">Berlin Plus agreement</a>. This is a comprehensive package of agreements made between NATO and the EU on 16 December 2002. With this agreement the EU is given the possibility to use NATO assets in case it wanted to act independently in an international crisis, on the condition that NATO does not want to act itself \xe2\x80\x93 the so-called "right of first refusal".<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a href="/wiki/File:European_defence_integration.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/European_defence_integration.svg/320px-European_defence_integration.svg.png" width="320" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/European_defence_integration.svg/480px-European_defence_integration.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/European_defence_integration.svg/640px-European_defence_integration.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="598" data-file-height="481" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:European_defence_integration.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The participation in European defence organisations</div></div></div>\n<p>In fact, many EU member states are among the 28 NATO members. The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brussels" title="Treaty of Brussels">Treaty of Brussels</a> is considered the precursor to NATO. The <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty" title="North Atlantic Treaty">North Atlantic Treaty</a> was signed in Washington, D.C. in 1949. It included the five Treaty of Brussels states, as well as the United States, Canada, Portugal, Italy, Norway, Denmark and Iceland. Greece and Turkey joined the alliance in 1952, and West Germany did the same in 1955. Spain entered in 1982. In 1999, Hungary, the Czech Republic, and Poland became NATO members. Finally, Bulgaria, Estonia, Latvia, Lithuania, Romania, Slovenia, and Slovakia joined in 2004. In 2009, Croatia and Albania joined. In 2008, Ukraine and Georgia were told that they will also eventually become members. The Republic of Macedonia\'s application process is finished, but it is blocked by Greece. Thus, 22 out of 28 NATO states are among the 28 EU members, another two are members of the EEA, and one more is an EU candidate and also a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">European Union Customs Union</a>.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Space">Space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:508px;max-width:508px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:252px;max-width:252px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Location_ESA_member_countries.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Location_ESA_member_countries.svg/250px-Location_ESA_member_countries.svg.png" width="250" height="210" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Location_ESA_member_countries.svg/375px-Location_ESA_member_countries.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Location_ESA_member_countries.svg/500px-Location_ESA_member_countries.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2045" data-file-height="1720" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #5B9ED7; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;ESA member countries</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #5FB4A1; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;ECS states</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #3D9345; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;signed Cooperation Agreement (CA)</div></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:252px;max-width:252px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:ESA_and_EU.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/ESA_and_EU.png/250px-ESA_and_EU.png" width="250" height="208" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/ESA_and_EU.png/375px-ESA_and_EU.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/ESA_and_EU.png/500px-ESA_and_EU.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1000" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #81c846; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;ESA and EU member countries</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #b94954; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;ESA-only members</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #3b54b1; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;EU-only members</div></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<dl><dd><i>For more information on ESA enlargement see also: <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Space_Agency" title="Enlargement of the European Space Agency">Enlargement of the European Space Agency</a></i></dd></dl>\n<p>On 22 May 2007, the member states of the European Union have agreed to create a common political framework for space activities in Europe by unifying the approach of the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a> (ESA) with those of the individual European Union member states.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>However, ESA is an intergovernmental organisation with no formal organic link to the EU; indeed the two institutions have different member states and are governed by different rules and procedures. ESA was created in 1975 by the merger of the two pre-existing European organisations engaged in space activities, <a href="/wiki/ELDO" class="mw-redirect" title="ELDO">ELDO</a> and <a href="/wiki/ESRO" class="mw-redirect" title="ESRO">ESRO</a>. The 10 founding members were Belgium, Denmark, France, Germany, Italy, the Netherlands, Spain, Sweden, Switzerland and the United Kingdom. Ireland joined on 31 December 1975. In 1987, Austria and Norway became member states. Finland joined in 1995, Portugal in 2000, Greece and Luxembourg in 2005, the Czech Republic in 2008, and Romania in 2011. Currently, it has 20 member states: all the EU member states before 2004, plus Czech Republic, Norway, Poland, Romania, and Switzerland. In addition, Canada has had the special status of a Cooperating State under a series of cooperation agreements dating since 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The political perspective of the European Union is to make ESA an <a href="/wiki/Agency_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Agency of the European Union">agency of the EU</a> by 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> ESA is likely to expand in the coming years with the countries which joined the EU in both 2004 and 2007. Currently, almost all EU member states are in different stages of affiliation with ESA. Poland<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> has joined on 19 November 2012. Hungary<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> and Estonia<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> have signed ESA Convention. Latvia and Slovenia have started to implement a Plan for European Cooperating State (PECS) Charter. Slovakia, Lithuania and Bulgaria have signed a European Cooperating State (ECS) Agreement. Cyprus,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Malta and Croatia have signed Cooperation Agreements with ESA.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership_in_European_Union_agreements">Membership in European Union agreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_integration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Membership in European Union agreements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EU-Agreements-2011-06-03.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/EU-Agreements-2011-06-03.svg/320px-EU-Agreements-2011-06-03.svg.png" width="320" height="269" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/EU-Agreements-2011-06-03.svg/480px-EU-Agreements-2011-06-03.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/EU-Agreements-2011-06-03.svg/640px-EU-Agreements-2011-06-03.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2045" data-file-height="1720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EU-Agreements-2011-06-03.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000080; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;EU, Schengen, EMU, CSDP (All agreements): 17 c.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #008080; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;EU, Schengen, CSDP: 4 c.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00FFFF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;EU, Schengen: 1 c.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #008000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;EU, EMU, CSDP: 2 c.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00FF00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;EU, CSDP: 3 c.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #800000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;EEA, Schengen: 2 c.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #803300; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Schengen, Bilateral treaties: 1 c.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF6600; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Candidates, some agreements: 5 c.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #F5FF52; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Microstates, some agreements: 5 c.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Association Agreement: 5 c.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:grey; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;some agreements: 0 c.</div></div></div></div>\n<dl><dd><i>For participation of non-EU countries in EU integration initiatives see also <a href="/wiki/Multi-speed_Europe#Participation_of_European_countries_in_EU_integration_initiatives" title="Multi-speed Europe">Multi-speed Europe</a></i></dd></dl>\n<p>A small group of EU member states have joined all European treaties, instead of opting out on some. They drive the development of a federal model for the European integration. This is linked to the concept of <a href="/wiki/Multi-speed_Europe" title="Multi-speed Europe">Multi-speed Europe</a> where some countries would create a core union; and goes back to the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Six" title="Inner Six">Inner Six</a> references to the founding member states of the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a>.\n</p><p>At present the formation of a formal Core Europe Federation ("a federation within the confederation") had been held off at every occasion that such a federation treaty had been discussed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Instead supranational institutions are created that govern more areas in "Inner Europe" than the existing European integration provides for.\n</p><p>Among the 28 EU state members, seventeen states have signed all integration agreements: Austria, Belgium, Finland, Estonia, France, Germany, Greece, Italy, Latvia, Lithuania, Luxembourg, Malta, Netherlands, Portugal, Slovakia, Slovenia and Spain.\n</p><p>The agreements considered include the fifth stage of economic integration or <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_Monetary_Union_of_the_European_Union" title="Economic and Monetary Union of the European Union">EMU</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Schengen agreement">Schengen agreement</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Common_Security_and_Defence_Policy" title="Common Security and Defence Policy">Common Security and Defence Policy</a>.\n</p><p>Thus, among the 28 EU countries, 19 have joined the Eurozone, 22 have joined Schengen, and 27 compose the European Military.\n</p><p>Further, some countries which do not belong to the EU have joined several of these initiatives, albeit sometimes at a lower stage such as the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">Customs Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">Common Market (EEA)</a>, or even unilaterally adopting the euro; by taking part in <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen</a>, either as a signatory state, or <i>de facto</i>; or by joining some common military forces.\n</p><p>Thus, six non-EU countries have adopted the euro (four through an agreement with the EU and two unilaterally), four non-EU states have joined the Schengen agreement officially, and other countries have joined common military corps.\n</p><p>The following table shows the status of each state membership to the different agreements promoted by the EU. It lists 45 countries, including the 28 EU member states, 5 candidate states, members of EEA (2 countries plus one EU candidate), 3 countries with some soft ties to the EU, such as those with SAA or participation agreements, as well as the 4 remaining Microstates (Liechtenstein is an EEA member) and Switzerland which has multiple bilateral treaties with the EU, as well as two Eastern Partner states.\n</p><p>Hence, this table summarises some components of EU laws applied in the European states. Some territories of EU member states also have a <a href="/wiki/Special_Member_State_territories_and_the_European_Union#Summary" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Member State territories and the European Union">special status</a> in regard to EU laws applied. Some territories of EFTA member states also have a <a href="/wiki/EFTA_and_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="EFTA and the European Union">special status</a> in regard to EU laws applied as is the case with some <a href="/wiki/Microstates_and_the_European_Union#Summary" title="Microstates and the European Union">European microstates</a>. For member states that do not have special-status territories the EU law applies fully with the exception of the <a href="/wiki/Opt-outs_in_the_European_Union" title="Opt-outs in the European Union">opt-outs in the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mechanism_for_Cooperation_and_Verification" title="Mechanism for Cooperation and Verification">states under a safeguard clause</a> or alternatively some states participate in <a href="/wiki/Enhanced_co-operation" class="mw-redirect" title="Enhanced co-operation">enhanced co-operation</a> between a subset of the EU members. Additionally there are various examples of non-participation by some EU members and non-EU states participation in particular <a href="/wiki/Agencies_of_the_European_Union" title="Agencies of the European Union">Agencies of the European Union</a>, the programmes for <a href="/wiki/European_Higher_Education_Area" title="European Higher Education Area">European Higher Education Area</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Research_Area" title="European Research Area">European Research Area</a> and <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Mundus" title="Erasmus Mundus">Erasmus Mundus</a>.\n</p>\n<table
